USA 111, 5135–5140 (2014)." href="/articles/s41438-020-00391-0#ref-CR12" id="ref-link-section-d16122e2494">12</a></sup>, tobacco<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 37" title="Sierro, N. et al. The tobacco genome sequence and its comparison with those of tomato and potato. Nat. Commun. 5, 3833 (2014)." href="/articles/s41438-020-00391-0#ref-CR37" id="ref-link-section-d16122e2498">37</a></sup>, petunia<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 38" title="Bombarely, A. et al. Insight into the evolution of the Solanaceae from the parental genomes of Petunia hybrid. Nat. Plants 2, 16074 (2016)." href="/articles/s41438-020-00391-0#ref-CR38" id="ref-link-section-d16122e2503">38</a></sup>, and four eggplants<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 13" title="Hirakawa, H. et al. Draft genome sequence of eggplant (Solanum melongena L.): the representative solanum species indigenous to the old world. DNA Res. 21, 649–660 (2014)." href="/articles/s41438-020-00391-0#ref-CR13" id="ref-link-section-d16122e2507">13</a>,<a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 16" title="Barchi, L. et al. A chromosome-anchored eggplant genome sequence reveals key events in Solanaceae evolution. Sci. Rep. 9, 11769 (2019)." href="/articles/s41438-020-00391-0#ref-CR16" id="ref-link-section-d16122e2510">16</a>,<a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 17" title="Song, B. et al. Draft genome sequence of Solanum aethiopicum provides insights into disease resistance, drought tolerance, and the evolution of the genome. GigaScience 8, 1–16 (2019)." href="/articles/s41438-020-00391-0#ref-CR17" id="ref-link-section-d16122e2513">17</a></sup> (<i>S. melongena</i>-HQ, <i>S. melongena</i>-NS, <i>S. melongena</i>-67/3, and <i>S. aethiopicum</i>). The Old World subgenus <i>Leptostemonum</i> comprises ~500 species and 30 sections, including half of the economically important crops<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 1" title="Chapman, M. A. The Eggplant Genome. (Springer Nature Switzerland AG, 2019)." href="/articles/s41438-020-00391-0#ref-CR1" id="ref-link-section-d16122e2533">1</a></sup>. The brinjal eggplant <i>S. melongena</i> belongs to section Melongena, whereas the closely related species, the scarlet eggplant <i>S. aethiopicum</i>, belongs to section Oliganthes. We found 6,087 gene families in common in the nine genomes, among which we identified 463 single-copy gene families (Fig. <a data-track="click" data-track-label="link" data-track-action="figure anchor" href="/articles/s41438-020-00391-0#Fig3">3</a>). <i>S. melongena</i> and <i>S. aethiopicum</i> diverged from each other ~2.4 Mya (Fig. S<a data-track="click" data-track-label="link" data-track-action="supplementary material anchor" href="/articles/s41438-020-00391-0#MOESM2">2</a>). In addition, comparative genomics were performed among three sequenced eggplant genomes, <i>S. melongena</i>-HQ, <i>S. melongena</i>-67/3 and <i>S. aethiopicum</i>, and three types of variations (SNPs, indels and SVs) were characterized. As expected, <i>S. melongena</i>-HQ has significantly higher numbers of SNPs (22,092,994), indels (1,988,560) and SVs (7362) when compared with <i>S. aethiopicum</i> than compared with <i>S. melongena</i>-67/3 (Fig. <a data-track="click" data-track-label="link" data-track-action="figure anchor" href="/articles/s41438-020-00391-0#Fig5">5</a>). SVs consist of deletions and insertions that may result in divergent gene expression and phenotypes<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" title="Carvalho, C. M. B. &amp; Lupski, J. R. Mechanisms underlying structural variant formation in genomic disorders. Nat. Rev. Genet. 17, 224–238 (2016)." href="#ref-CR39" id="ref-link-section-d16122e2578">39</a>,<a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" title="Cook, D. E. et al. Missing heritability and strategies for finding the underlying causes of complex disease. Nat. Rev. Genet. 11, 446–450 (2010)." href="#ref-CR40" id="ref-link-section-d16122e2578_1">40</a>,<a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" title="Chakraborty, M. et al. Hidden genetic variation shapes the structure of functional elements in Drosophila. Nat. Genet. 50, 20–25 (2018)." href="#ref-CR41" id="ref-link-section-d16122e2578_2">41</a>,<a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 42" title="Yin, D. M. et al. Comparison of Arachis monticola with diploid and cultivated tetraploid genomes reveals asymmetric subgenome evolution and improvement of peanut. Adv. Sci. 7, 1901672 (2019)." href="/articles/s41438-020-00391-0#ref-CR42" id="ref-link-section-d16122e2581">42</a></sup>. Interestingly, asymmetric SV accumulation was found in potential regulatory regions of protein-coding genes among the different eggplants, with more deletions than insertions between <i>S. melongena</i>-HQ and <i>S. aethiopicum</i>. In contrast similar insertion and deletion levels were observed between the two <i>S. melongena</i> genomes. This phenomenon has also been detected between two subgenomes of the allotetraploid peanut<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 42" title="Yin, D. M. et al. Comparison of Arachis monticola with diploid and cultivated tetraploid genomes reveals asymmetric subgenome evolution and improvement of peanut. Adv. Sci. 7, 1901672 (2019)." href="/articles/s41438-020-00391-0#ref-CR42" id="ref-link-section-d16122e2595">42</a></sup>. Overall the genome sequence of the linear eggplant HQ-1315 and comparative genomic information of <i>S. melongena</i> with that of related species allowed for the identification of genomic divergence at the whole-genome level, and the findings provide genomic tools for the improvement of agronomic traits in eggplant.</p><p>Stress resistance and fruit morphology (i.e., shape and color) are important traits during eggplant domestication that are vastly different among cultivated <i>S. melongena</i> varieties and closely related species. <i>S. aethiopicum</i> is mostly grown in tropical Africa, with outstanding disease resistance to various pathogens, such as <i>Fusarium</i> and <i>Verticillium</i> and is cross-compatible with <i>S. melongena</i><sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 43" title="Prohens, J. et al. Characterization of interspecific hybrids and first backcross generations from crosses between two cultivated eggplants (Solanum melongenaand S. aethiopicum Kumba group) and implications for eggplant breeding. Euphytica 186, 517–538 (2012)." href="/articles/s41438-020-00391-0#ref-CR43" id="ref-link-section-d16122e2619">43</a>,<a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 44" title="Collonnier, C. et al. Source of resistance against Ralstonia solanacearum in fertile somatic hybrids of eggplant (Solanum melongena L.) with Solanum aethiopicum L. Plant Sci. 160, 301–313 (2001)." href="/articles/s41438-020-00391-0#ref-CR44" id="ref-link-section-d16122e2622">44</a></sup>. We identified 301 NBS-LRR genes in <i>S. melongena</i>-HQ and 250 NBS-LRR genes in <i>S. melongena</i>-67/3. As expected, <i>S. aethiopicum</i> has a higher number of disease resistance genes, with 436 genes involved in ten types. <i>S. melongena</i>-NS (Japanese eggplant) and <i>S. melongena</i>-67/3 (European eggplant) both have dark-purple fruits, with elliptical, oval or round shapes, whereas <i>S. melongena</i>-HQ has unusually linear-shaped fruits with a bright-purple color (Fig. <a data-track="click" data-track-label="link" data-track-action="figure anchor" href="/articles/s41438-020-00391-0#Fig1">1</a>). We constructed an F<sub>2</sub> segregating population and performed QTL mapping analysis on eggplant fruit length using the <i>S. melongena</i>-HQ genome (Fig. <a data-track="click" data-track-label="link" data-track-action="figure anchor" href="/articles/s41438-020-00391-0#Fig7">7</a>). A QTL interval for fruit length was identified within a 71.29–78.26-Mb region on chromosome E03, with a 99% confidence interval. Gene prediction was conducted by homology comparison based on the syntenic relationship between eggplant and tomato, which yielded 11 homologous genes for fruit size on eggplant chromosome E03. Combining these results with the identification of the QTL region <i>FS3.1</i> in our previous study<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 30" title="Wei, Q. Z. et al. Construction of a SNP-Based genetic map using SLAF-Seq and QTL analysis of morphological traits in eggplant. Front. Genet. 11, 178 (2020)." href="/articles/s41438-020-00391-0#ref-CR30" id="ref-link-section-d16122e2660">30</a></sup>, we propose that <i>Smechr0301963</i> (the ortholog from <i>S. melongena</i>-67/3 is <i>SMEL_003g182360</i>), a gene potentially orthologous to <i>SUN</i> gene family members, is a key candidate gene for regulating eggplant fruit length.</p><p>Eggplant research is far behind that of other Solanaceae crops (i.e., tomatoes, peppers, and potatoes) and important crops such as cucumber. For QTL mapping research, previous studies have often used tomato genomes for collinear comparisons because of the lack of high-quality eggplant reference genomes<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" title="Cericola, F. et al. Linkage disequilibrium and genome-wide association analysis for anthocyanin pigmentation and fruit color in eggplant. BMC Genomics 15, 896 (2014)." href="#ref-CR25" id="ref-link-section-d16122e2680">25</a>,<a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" title="Portis, E. et al. QTL mapping in eggplant reveals clusters of yield-related loci and orthology with the tomato genome. PLoS ONE 9, e89499 (2014)." href="#ref-CR26" id="ref-link-section-d16122e2680_1">26</a>,<a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 27" title="Portis, E. et al. Association mapping for fruit, plant and leaf morphology traits in eggplant. PLoS ONE 10, e0135200 (2015)." href="/articles/s41438-020-00391-0#ref-CR27" id="ref-link-section-d16122e2683">27</a>,<a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 45" title="Frary, A. et al. QTL hotspots in eggplant (Solanum melongena) detected with a high resolution map and CIM analysis. Euphytica 197, 211–228 (2014)." href="/articles/s41438-020-00391-0#ref-CR45" id="ref-link-section-d16122e2686">45</a>,<a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 46" title="Fukuoka, H. et al. Development of gene-based markers and construction of an integrated linkage map in eggplant by using Solanum orthologous (SOL) gene sets. Theor. Appl. Genet. 125, 47–56 (2012)." href="/articles/s41438-020-00391-0#ref-CR46" id="ref-link-section-d16122e2689">46</a></sup>. Our study provides a high-quality eggplant genome that has wide applications in eggplant genetics and genomics studies, such as marker development, gene detection and chromosome evolution. In the present study, we detected QTL hotspots based on published QTL mapping results and marker information<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" title="Barchi, L. et al. A RAD tag derived marker based eggplant linkage map and the location of QTLs determining anthocyanin pigmentation. PLoS ONE 7, e43740 (2012)." href="#ref-CR23" id="ref-link-section-d16122e2693">23</a>,<a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" title="Barchi, L. et al. QTL analysis reveals new eggplant loci involved in resistance to fungal wilts. Euphytica 214, 20 (2018)." href="#ref-CR24" id="ref-link-section-d16122e2693_1">24</a>,<a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" title="Cericola, F. et al. Linkage disequilibrium and genome-wide association analysis for anthocyanin pigmentation and fruit color in eggplant. BMC Genomics 15, 896 (2014)." href="#ref-CR25" id="ref-link-section-d16122e2693_2">25</a>,<a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" title="Portis, E. et al. QTL mapping in eggplant reveals clusters of yield-related loci and orthology with the tomato genome. PLoS ONE 9, e89499 (2014)." href="#ref-CR26" id="ref-link-section-d16122e2693_3">26</a>,<a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" title="Portis, E. et al. Association mapping for fruit, plant and leaf morphology traits in eggplant. PLoS ONE 10, e0135200 (2015)." href="#ref-CR27" id="ref-link-section-d16122e2693_4">27</a>,<a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" title="Toppino, L. et al. Mapping quantitative trait loci affecting biochemical and morphological fruit properties in eggplant (Solanum melongena L.). Front. Plant Sci. 4, 256 (2016)." href="#ref-CR28" id="ref-link-section-d16122e2693_5">28</a>,<a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" title="Miyatake, K. et al. Detailed mapping of a resistance locus against Fusarium wilt in cultivated eggplant (Solanum melongena L.). Theor. Appl. Genet. 129, 357–367 (2016)." href="#ref-CR29" id="ref-link-section-d16122e2693_6">29</a>,<a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 30" title="Wei, Q. Z. et al. Construction of a SNP-Based genetic map using SLAF-Seq and QTL analysis of morphological traits in eggplant. Front. Genet. 11, 178 (2020)." href="/articles/s41438-020-00391-0#ref-CR30" id="ref-link-section-d16122e2696">30</a></sup>, with 210 markers associated with 71 traits anchored to the <i>S. melongena</i>-HQ reference genome (Fig. <a data-track="click" data-track-label="link" data-track-action="figure anchor" href="/articles/s41438-020-00391-0#Fig8">8</a>; Supplementary Table S<a data-track="click" data-track-label="link" data-track-action="supplementary material anchor" href="/articles/s41438-020-00391-0#MOESM15">10</a>). We identified and summarized 26 QTL hotspots, providing a valuable reference and basis for further exploration of regulatory genes controlling important traits in eggplant.</p></div></div></section><section aria-labelledby="Sec12" data-title="Materials and methods"><div class="c-article-section" id="Sec12-section"><h2 class="c-article-section__title js-section-title js-c-reading-companion-sections-item" id="Sec12">Materials and methods</h2><div class="c-article-section__content" id="Sec12-content"><h3 class="c-article__sub-heading" id="Sec13">Plant materials, DNA extraction, and genome sequencing</h3><p>The eggplant cultivar HQ-1315 was selected for whole-genome sequencing; it is a high-generation self-crossbred inbred line with elongated purple fruits. HQ-1315 is an important parental material derived from the Vegetable Institute of Zhejiang Academy of Agricultural Sciences. The HQ-1315 plants were grown in a greenhouse at Qiaosi of Zhejiang Academy of Agricultural Sciences (Hangzhou, China) under standard conditions. DNA was extracted from the young leaves of HQ-1315 for genome sequencing using DNA Secure Plant Kit (TIANGEN, China) and broken into random fragments. Four kinds of DNA sequencing libraries were constructed, including a 350-bp insert size library, Nanopore library, 10× Genomics library, and Hi-C library, according to the manufacturers’ instructions. The genome was sequenced using Illumina NovaSeq PE150 and Nanopore PromethION according to standard Illumina (Illumina, CA, USA) and Nanopore (Oxford Nanopore Technologies) protocols at Novogene.</p><p>To estimate the eggplant genome size, k-mer distribution analysis was used, and 17-nt k-mers were employed to determine abundance with 93.33 Gb of paired-end reads. SOAPdenovo software was used to splice and assemble the reads into scaffolds with 41-nt k-mers.</p><h3 class="c-article__sub-heading c-article__sub-heading--divider" id="Sec14">Genome assembly and evaluation</h3><p>We used wtdbg2 software<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 47" title="Ruan, J. &amp; Li, H. Fast and accurate long-read assembly with wtdbg2. Nat. Methods 17, 1–4 (2020)." href="/articles/s41438-020-00391-0#ref-CR47" id="ref-link-section-d16122e2732">47</a></sup> to assemble the noncleaned raw reads from Nanopore sequencing according to the Fuzzy Bruijn Graph (FBG) algorithm. To derive each point, a 1024-bp sequence was selected from the reads, and the points were connected to construct the FBG figure using gapped sequence alignments. Finally, a consensus sequence was obtained. We polished the consensus sequence three times with Nanopore reads using Racon software<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 48" title="Vaser, R., Sovic, I., Nagarajan, N. &amp; Sikic, M. Fast and accurate de novo genome assembly from long uncorrected reads. Genome Res. 27, 737–746 (2017)." href="/articles/s41438-020-00391-0#ref-CR48" id="ref-link-section-d16122e2736">48</a></sup>. The split size was 50, and the other parameters were set to defaults. Paired-end clean reads obtained from the Illumina platform were aligned to the eggplant assembly using BWA software<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 49" title="Li, H. &amp; Durbin, R. Fast and accurate short read alignment with Burrows–Wheeler transform. Bioinformatics 25, 1754–1760 (2009)." href="/articles/s41438-020-00391-0#ref-CR49" id="ref-link-section-d16122e2740">49</a></sup> (v0.7.17). Postprocessing error correction and conflict resolution of the assembly were performed using the Pilon tool with default parameters. The fragScaff software<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 50" title="Mostovoy, Y. et al. A hybrid approach for de novo human genome sequence assembly and phasing. Nat. Methods 13, 587–590 (2016)." href="/articles/s41438-020-00391-0#ref-CR50" id="ref-link-section-d16122e2744">50</a></sup> was applied for 10X Genomics scaffold extension. Linked reads generated from the 10X Genomics library were aligned to the consensus sequence of the Nanopore assembly to obtain long scaffolds. The consensus sequences were filtered, and only those with linked-read support were used for subsequent assembly. Then, clean Hi-C data were aligned to the primary draft assembly using BWA software v0.7.17<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 49" title="Li, H. &amp; Durbin, R. Fast and accurate short read alignment with Burrows–Wheeler transform. Bioinformatics 25, 1754–1760 (2009)." href="/articles/s41438-020-00391-0#ref-CR49" id="ref-link-section-d16122e2748">49</a></sup>. SAMtools<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 51" title="Li, H. et al. 1000 Genome Project Data Processing Subgroup. The Sequence Alignment/Map format and SAMtools. Bioinformatics 25, 2078–2079 (2009)." href="/articles/s41438-020-00391-0#ref-CR51" id="ref-link-section-d16122e2753">51</a></sup> was utilized to remove duplicates and nonaligned reads, and only read pairs with both reads in the pair aligned to contigs were considered for scaffolding. Ultimately, 12 superscaffolds (pseudochromosomes) were assembled from corrected contigs using LACHESIS software<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 52" title="Burton, J. N. et al. Chromosome-scale scaffolding of de novo genome assemblies based on chromatin interactions. Nat. Biotechnol. 31, 1119–1125 (2013)." href="/articles/s41438-020-00391-0#ref-CR52" id="ref-link-section-d16122e2757">52</a></sup>.</p><p>To evaluate the accuracy of the assembly, short reads were blast searched against the genome using BWA software<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 49" title="Li, H. &amp; Durbin, R. Fast and accurate short read alignment with Burrows–Wheeler transform. Bioinformatics 25, 1754–1760 (2009)." href="/articles/s41438-020-00391-0#ref-CR49" id="ref-link-section-d16122e2764">49</a></sup>. CEGMA (<a href="http://korflab.ucdavis.edu/datasets/cegma/">http://korflab.ucdavis.edu/datasets/cegma/</a>) was used to assess the completeness of the eggplant genome assembly, and BUSCO v4<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 53" title="Simão, F. A. et al. BUSCO: assessing genome assembly and annotation completeness with single-copy orthologs. Bioinformatics 31, 3210–3212 (2015)." href="/articles/s41438-020-00391-0#ref-CR53" id="ref-link-section-d16122e2775">53</a></sup> analysis was performed to further evaluate the assembled genome.</p><h3 class="c-article__sub-heading c-article__sub-heading--divider" id="Sec15">Transcriptome sequencing and gene annotation</h3><p>HQ-1315 plants were grown in a greenhouse at Qiaosi of Zhejiang Academy of Agricultural Sciences (Hangzhou, China) under standard conditions. RNA from five different tissues (root, stem, leaf, flower, and fruit) was extracted for next-generation transcriptome sequencing and full-length transcriptome sequencing using Illumina NovaSeq PE150 as an auxiliary annotation. Transcriptome read assemblies were generated with Trinity<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 54" title="Grabherr, M. G. et al. Full-length transcriptome assembly from RNA-Seq data without a reference genome. Nat. Biotechnol. 29, 644–652 (2011)." href="/articles/s41438-020-00391-0#ref-CR54" id="ref-link-section-d16122e2787">54</a></sup> (v2.1.1) for gene annotation.</p><p>To optimize the gene annotation, RNA-seq reads from different tissues were aligned to genome fasta sequences using TopHat<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 55" title="Kim, D. et al. TopHat2: accurate alignment of transcriptomes in the presence of insertions, deletions and gene fusions. Genome Biol. 14, R36 (2013)." href="/articles/s41438-020-00391-0#ref-CR55" id="ref-link-section-d16122e2794">55</a></sup> (v2.0.11) with the default parameters to identify exon regions and splice positions. The alignment results were then applied as input for Cufflinks<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 56" title="Trapnell, C. et al. Transcript assembly and quantification by RNA-Seq reveals unannotated transcripts and isoform switching during cell differentiation. Nat. Biotechnol. 28, 511–515 (2010)." href="/articles/s41438-020-00391-0#ref-CR56" id="ref-link-section-d16122e2798">56</a></sup> (v2.2.1) with default parameters for genome-based transcript assembly. A nonredundant reference gene set was generated by merging genes predicted by three methods with EvidenceModeler<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 57" title="Haas, B. J. et al. Automated eukaryotic gene structure annotation using evidencemodeler and the program to assemble spliced alignments. Genome Biol. 9, R7 (2008)." href="/articles/s41438-020-00391-0#ref-CR57" id="ref-link-section-d16122e2802">57</a></sup> (EVM, v1.1.1) using PASA<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 58" title="Campbell, M. A., Hass, B. J., Hamilton, J. P., Mount, S. M. &amp; Buell, C. R. Comprehensive analysis of alternative splicing in rice and comparative analyses with Arabidopsis. BMC Genom. 7, 1–7 (2006)." href="/articles/s41438-020-00391-0#ref-CR58" id="ref-link-section-d16122e2806">58</a></sup> (Program to Assemble Spliced Alignment) terminal exon support and including masked transposable elements as gene prediction input.</p><p>For ab initio gene annotation, Augustus<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 59" title="Stanke, M., Steinkamp, R., Waack, S. &amp; Morgenstern, B. AUGUSTUS: a web server for gene finding in eukaryotes. Nucleic Acids Res. 32, 309–312 (2004)." href="/articles/s41438-020-00391-0#ref-CR59" id="ref-link-section-d16122e2813">59</a></sup> (v3.2.3), GeneID<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 60" title="Parra, G., Blanco, E. &amp; Guigó, R. GeneID in Drosophila. Genome Res. 10, 511 (2000)." href="/articles/s41438-020-00391-0#ref-CR60" id="ref-link-section-d16122e2817">60</a></sup> (v1.4), GeneScan<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 61" title="Aggarwal, G. &amp; Ramaswamy, R. Ab initio gene identification: prokaryote genome annotation with GeneScan and GLIMMER. J. Biosci. 27, 7–14 (2002)." href="/articles/s41438-020-00391-0#ref-CR61" id="ref-link-section-d16122e2821">61</a></sup> (v1.0), GlimmerHMM<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 62" title="Majoros, W. H., Pertea, M. &amp; Salzberg, S. L. TigrScan and GlimmerHMM: two open source ab initio eukaryotic gene-finders. Bioinformatics 20, 2878–2879 (2004)." href="/articles/s41438-020-00391-0#ref-CR62" id="ref-link-section-d16122e2825">62</a></sup> (v3.04), and SNAP<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 63" title="Bromberg, Y. &amp; Rost, B. SNAP: predict effect of non-synonymous polymorphisms on function. Nucleic Acids Res. 35, 3823 (2007)." href="/articles/s41438-020-00391-0#ref-CR63" id="ref-link-section-d16122e2829">63</a></sup> were used in the automated gene prediction pipeline. Individual families of interest were selected for further manual curation by relevant experts. For structural annotation, ab initio prediction, homology-based prediction, and RNA-seq assisted prediction were used to annotate gene models.</p><h3 class="c-article__sub-heading c-article__sub-heading--divider" id="Sec16">Repeat annotation</h3><p>A combined strategy based on homology alignment and a de novo search was used in the repeat annotation pipeline to identify repetitive elements in the eggplant genome. Tandem repeats were extracted using TRF (<a href="http://tandem.bu.edu/trf/trf.html">http://tandem.bu.edu/trf/trf.html</a>) by ab initio prediction. For homolog-based prediction, the Repbase TE library and TE protein database were employed to search against the eggplant genome using RepeatMasker<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 64" title="Smit, A. F. A., Hubley, R. &amp; Green, P. RepeatMasker Open-4.0. &#xA;                  http://www.repeatmasker.org&#xA;                  &#xA;                 (1996–2013)." href="/articles/s41438-020-00391-0#ref-CR64" id="ref-link-section-d16122e2848">64</a></sup> (version 4.0) and RepeatProteinMask, respectively, with the default parameters. For de novo-based approach prediction, a de novo repetitive element database was built with LTR_FINDER<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 65" title="Xu, Z. &amp; Wang, H. LTR_FINDER: an efficient tool for the prediction of full-length LTR retrotransposons. Nucleic Acids Res. 35, 265–268 (2007)." href="/articles/s41438-020-00391-0#ref-CR65" id="ref-link-section-d16122e2852">65</a></sup>, RepeatScout<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 66" title="Price, A. L., Jones, N. C. &amp; Pevzner, P. A. De novo identification of repeat families in large genomes. Bioinformatics 21, 351–358 (2005)." href="/articles/s41438-020-00391-0#ref-CR66" id="ref-link-section-d16122e2856">66</a></sup>, and RepeatModeler<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 67" title="Smit, A. F. A. &amp; Hubley, R. RepeatModeler Open-1.0. &#xA;                  http://www.repeatmasker.org&#xA;                  &#xA;                 (2008–2015)." href="/articles/s41438-020-00391-0#ref-CR67" id="ref-link-section-d16122e2860">67</a></sup>, also with default parameters.</p><h3 class="c-article__sub-heading c-article__sub-heading--divider" id="Sec17">Homolog prediction</h3><p>A total of five species were included in homolog prediction: <i>S. tuberosum</i>, <i>S. melongena</i>, <i>S. lycopersicum</i>, <i>C. annuum</i>, and <i>N. tabacum</i>. Sequences of homologous proteins were downloaded from NCBI and aligned to the genome using tBlastn<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 68" title="Altschul, S. F. et al. Gapped BLAST and PSI-BLAST: a new generation of protein database search programs. Nucleic Acids Res. 25, 3389–3402 (1997)." href="/articles/s41438-020-00391-0#ref-CR68" id="ref-link-section-d16122e2889">68</a></sup> (v2.2.26; <i>E</i>-value ≤ 1e − 5). The matching proteins were then aligned to the homologous genome sequences using GeneWise<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 69" title="Birney, E., Clamp, M. &amp; Durbin, R. GeneWise and Genomewise. Genome Res. 14, 988–995 (2004)." href="/articles/s41438-020-00391-0#ref-CR69" id="ref-link-section-d16122e2896">69</a></sup> (v2.4.1) software to produce accurate spliced alignments, which were applied to predict the gene structure contained in each protein region.</p><h3 class="c-article__sub-heading c-article__sub-heading--divider" id="Sec18">Functional annotation</h3><p>The functions of protein-coding genes were assigned according to the best match by aligning the protein sequences against the Swiss-Prot database using Blastp<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 70" title="Gish, W. &amp; States, D. J. Identification of protein coding regions by database similarity search. Nat. Genet. 3, 266–272 (1993)." href="/articles/s41438-020-00391-0#ref-CR70" id="ref-link-section-d16122e2908">70</a></sup>, with a threshold of <i>E</i>-value ≤ 1e<sup>−5</sup>. Protein motifs and domains were annotated by searching against the ProDom<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 71" title="Gouzy, J. et al. XDOM, a graphical tool to analyse domain arrangements in any set of protein sequences. CABIOS 13, 601–608 (1997)." href="/articles/s41438-020-00391-0#ref-CR71" id="ref-link-section-d16122e2917">71</a></sup>, Pfam<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 72" title="Finn, R. D. et al. Pfam: the protein families database. Nat. Genet. 42, 222–230 (2014)." href="/articles/s41438-020-00391-0#ref-CR72" id="ref-link-section-d16122e2921">72</a></sup> (V27.0), SMRT<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 73" title="Letunic, I. et al. SMART 4.0: towards genomic data integration. Nucleic Acids Res. 32, 142–144 (2004)." href="/articles/s41438-020-00391-0#ref-CR73" id="ref-link-section-d16122e2926">73</a></sup>, PANTHER<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 74" title="Mi, H. Y., Muruganujan, A. &amp; Thomas, P. D. PANTHER in 2013: modeling the evolution of gene function, and other gene attributes, in the context of phylogenetic trees. Nucleic Acids Res. 41, 377–386 (2012)." href="/articles/s41438-020-00391-0#ref-CR74" id="ref-link-section-d16122e2930">74</a></sup>, and PROSITE<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 75" title="Sigrist, C. J. A. et al. New and continuing developments at PROSITE. Nucleic Acids Res. 41, 344–347 (2013)." href="/articles/s41438-020-00391-0#ref-CR75" id="ref-link-section-d16122e2934">75</a></sup> databases using InterProScan<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 76" title="Hunter, S. et al. InterPro: the integrative protein signature database. Nucleic Acids Res. 37, 211–215 (2009)." href="/articles/s41438-020-00391-0#ref-CR76" id="ref-link-section-d16122e2938">76</a></sup> (v5.31). GO IDs<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 77" title="Ashburner, M. et al. Gene ontology: tool for the unification of biology. The Gene Ontology Consortium. Nat. Genet. 25, 25–29 (2000)." href="/articles/s41438-020-00391-0#ref-CR77" id="ref-link-section-d16122e2942">77</a></sup> for each gene were assigned according to the corresponding InterPro entry. Protein functions were predicted by transferring annotations from the closest BLAST hit (<i>E</i>-value &lt; 10<sup>−5</sup>) in the Swiss-Prot and NR databases. We also assigned a gene set to the KEGG pathway database<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 78" title="Kanehisa, M. et al. Data, information, knowledge and principle: back to metabolism in KEGG. Nucleic Acids Res. 42, 199–205 (2014)." href="/articles/s41438-020-00391-0#ref-CR78" id="ref-link-section-d16122e2952">78</a></sup> (release 53) and identified the best matched pathway for each gene.</p><h3 class="c-article__sub-heading c-article__sub-heading--divider" id="Sec19">Noncoding RNA annotation</h3><p>tRNAs were predicted using tRNAscan-SE software<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 79" title="Lowe, T. M. &amp; Eddy, S. R. tRNAscan-SE: a program for improved detection of transfer RNA genes in genomic sequence. Nucleic Acids Res. 25, 955–964 (1997)." href="/articles/s41438-020-00391-0#ref-CR79" id="ref-link-section-d16122e2964">79</a></sup> (<a href="http://lowelab.ucsc.edu/tRNAscan-SE/">http://lowelab.ucsc.edu/tRNAscan-SE/</a>). rRNAs were identified by alignment to the rRNA sequences of related species using BLASTN. Other noncoding RNAs, including miRNAs and snRNAs, were identified by searching against the Rfam database<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 80" title="Griffiths-Jones, S. et al. Rfam: annotating non-codin RNAs in complete genomes. Nucleic Acids Res. 33, 121–124 (2005)." href="/articles/s41438-020-00391-0#ref-CR80" id="ref-link-section-d16122e2975">80</a></sup> (release 9.1) using INFERNAL software<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 81" title="Nawrocki, E. P., Kolbe, D. L. &amp; Eddy, S. R. Infernal 1.0: inference of RNA alignments. Bioinformatics 25, 1335 (2009)." href="/articles/s41438-020-00391-0#ref-CR81" id="ref-link-section-d16122e2979">81</a></sup> (<a href="http://infernal.janelia.org/">http://infernal.janelia.org/</a>).</p><h3 class="c-article__sub-heading c-article__sub-heading--divider" id="Sec20">Gene family construction and expansion/contraction analysis</h3><p>Protein sequences predicted from the <i>S. melongena</i>-HQ eggplant genome and eight other sequenced Solanaceae genomes, <i>S. tuberosum</i>, <i>S. lycopersicum</i>, <i>S. melongena</i>-NS, <i>S. melongena</i>-67/3, <i>S. aethiopicum</i>, <i>C. annuum</i>, <i>P. inflata,</i> and <i>N. tabacum</i>, were used for gene family clustering. The gene set from each species was filtered according to the three steps described by Sun et al.<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 13" title="Hirakawa, H. et al. Draft genome sequence of eggplant (Solanum melongena L.): the representative solanum species indigenous to the old world. DNA Res. 21, 649–660 (2014)." href="/articles/s41438-020-00391-0#ref-CR13" id="ref-link-section-d16122e3026">13</a></sup>, with slight changes. The genes encoding proteins of fewer than 50 amino acids were filtered out. The gene families of the four eggplant genomes (<i>S. melongena</i>-HQ <i>S. melongena</i>-NS, <i>S. melongena</i>-67/3, and <i>S. aethiopicum</i>) were extracted for Venn diagram analysis to identify species-specific gene families in <i>S. melongena</i>-HQ. GO and KEGG annotation was performed to investigate the functions of those species-specific genes.</p><p>The expansion and contraction of gene families were analyzed by comparing family sizes between the MRCA and each of the nine sequenced Solanaceae genomes using CAFE<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 82" title="Han, M. V., Thomas, G. W., Lugo-Martinez, J. &amp; Hahn, M. W. Estimating gene gain and loss rates in the presence of error in genome assembly and annotation using CAFE 3. Mol. Biol. Evol. 30, 1987–1997 (2013)." href="/articles/s41438-020-00391-0#ref-CR82" id="ref-link-section-d16122e3049">82</a></sup>. The corresponding <i>p</i>-value for each lineage was calculated using conditional likelihoods, and families with a <i>p</i>-value of 0.05 were considered significantly expanded or contracted. The expanded and contracted genes were also analysed by GO and KEGG annotation.</p><h3 class="c-article__sub-heading c-article__sub-heading--divider" id="Sec21">Phylogenetic analysis</h3><p>MUSCLE<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 83" title="Edgar, R. C. MUSCLE: multiple sequence alignment with high accuracy and high throughput. Nucleic Acids Res. 32, 1792–1797 (2004)." href="/articles/s41438-020-00391-0#ref-CR83" id="ref-link-section-d16122e3067">83</a></sup> (<a href="http://www.drive5.com/muscle/">http://www.drive5.com/muscle/</a>) was used to align single-copy genes from representative Solanaceae genomes, and the results were combined to generate a superalignment matrix. Using RAxML<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 84" title="Stamatakis, A. RAxML version 8: a tool for phylogenetic analysis and postanalysis of large phylogenies. Bioinformatics 30, 1312–1313 (2014)." href="/articles/s41438-020-00391-0#ref-CR84" id="ref-link-section-d16122e3078">84</a></sup> (<a href="http://sco.h-its.org/exelixis/web/software/raxml/index.html">http://sco.h-its.org/exelixis/web/software/raxml/index.html</a>), a phylogenetic tree of the nine sequenced Solanaceae genomes was constructed with the maximum likelihood (ML) algorithm and 1000 bootstrap replicates. <i>P. inflata</i> was designated as the outgroup. To determine divergence times based on the phylogenetic tree, the MCMCTree program implemented in PAML5 software<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 85" title="Yang, Z. H. PAML 4: phylogenetic analysis by maximum likelihood. Mol. Biol. Evol. 24, 1586–1591 (2007)." href="/articles/s41438-020-00391-0#ref-CR85" id="ref-link-section-d16122e3093">85</a></sup> was used. Divergence time calibration information was obtained from the TimeTree database (<a href="http://www.time.org/">http://www.time.org/</a>).</p><h3 class="c-article__sub-heading c-article__sub-heading--divider" id="Sec22">Detection of WGD events</h3><p>Protein sequences from <i>S. melongena-HQ</i>, <i>S. aethiopicum</i>, <i>S. lycopersicum</i>, <i>S. tuberosum</i>, <i>C. annuum</i>, and <i>A. thaliana</i> were used for BLASTP (<i>E</i>-value &lt; 1e−05) searches within or between genomes to identify syntenic blocks, after which syntenic blocks were searched using MCScanX (<a href="http://chibba.pgml.uga.edu/mcscan2/">http://chibba.pgml.uga.edu/mcscan2/</a>) software according to the locations of the genes and the blast results. Muscle multiple sequence alignment was performed on the paralogous genes in the syntenic blocks, and the results of the protein alignment were used as templates to generate CDS alignment results. Finally, 4DTv values were calculated according to the comparison results, and a frequency distribution diagram of the 4DTv values and gene pairs was drawn.</p><h3 class="c-article__sub-heading c-article__sub-heading--divider" id="Sec23">Chromosome collinearity analysis</h3><p>The CDSs of two species in the comparison group were compared with BLAST software (<a href="http://last.cbrc.jp/">http://last.cbrc.jp/</a>), and JCVI was employed to locate syntenic blocks and map them with the following parameters: —cScore=0.9, —minspan=30, (<a href="https://github.com/">https://github.com/</a> tanghaibao/jcvi/wiki/MCscan- Python - version).</p><h3 class="c-article__sub-heading c-article__sub-heading--divider" id="Sec24">Identification of SNPs, indels, and SVs</h3><p>The genome sequence of <i>S. melongena</i>-HQ was aligned to that of <i>S. melongena</i>-67/3 and <i>S. aethiopicum</i> using BWA v0.7.17<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 49" title="Li, H. &amp; Durbin, R. Fast and accurate short read alignment with Burrows–Wheeler transform. Bioinformatics 25, 1754–1760 (2009)." href="/articles/s41438-020-00391-0#ref-CR49" id="ref-link-section-d16122e3181">49</a></sup> using default parameters. Picard tools v1.9.4 (<a href="https://broadinstitute.github.io/picard/">https://broadinstitute.github.io/picard/</a>) was applied to sort the alignment result sequence alignment map (SAM) files. SNPs and indels were called using Genome Analysis Toolkit<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 86" title="McKenna, A. et al. The Genome Analysis Toolkit: a MapReduce framework for analyzing next-generation DNA sequencing data. Genome Res. 20, 1297–1303 (2010)." href="/articles/s41438-020-00391-0#ref-CR86" id="ref-link-section-d16122e3193">86</a></sup>, and related genes were called according to genome position using an in-house Perl script.</p><p>Clean reads of <i>S. melongena</i>-HQ were aligned to those of <i>S. melongena</i>-67/3 and <i>S. aethiopicum</i> using BWA v0.7.17<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 49" title="Li, H. &amp; Durbin, R. Fast and accurate short read alignment with Burrows–Wheeler transform. Bioinformatics 25, 1754–1760 (2009)." href="/articles/s41438-020-00391-0#ref-CR49" id="ref-link-section-d16122e3209">49</a></sup> with default parameters. BreakDancerMax-0.0.1r61 was used for genome-wide detection of SVs with default parameters<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 87" title="Chen, K. et al. Breakdancer: an algorithm for high-resolution mapping of genomic structural variation. Nat. Methods 6, 677–681 (2009)." href="/articles/s41438-020-00391-0#ref-CR87" id="ref-link-section-d16122e3213">87</a></sup>. Deletion and insertion structure variations &lt;10 bp or &gt;10 kb in length were discarded. For the identification of SV genes, any gene with SVs in the main body or upstream/downstream regions was defined as an SV gene; otherwise, it was defined as a non-SV gene.</p><h3 class="c-article__sub-heading c-article__sub-heading--divider" id="Sec25">Identification of the NBS gene family and transcription factors</h3><p>Most NBS-encoding genes in eggplant were identified based on NB-ARC (NBS) conserved domains that are shared within the gene family and have relatively conserved NBS domains. The latest Markov model for the NBS transcription factor PF00931 was downloaded from the Pfam database (<a href="http://pfam.xfam.org/">http://pfam.xfam.org/</a>). The HMMER program was used to search for proteins containing this domain against the annotated protein database using the PF00931 domain as a query, with a cutoff <i>E</i>-value of 1e−4. To annotate the maximum number of NBS genes in the genomes, we also used the obtained NBS protein sequences for homologous annotation of genome sequences. tBlastn was applied for homology comparison, and the upper and lower segments of the comparison region were expanded by 5 kb each. Genewise software was then used for gene structure prediction, and homologous protein sequences were screened with PF00931. For the identification of transcription factors, iTAK-1.5-alpha software was utilized to predict transcription factors among the longest transcribed translated protein sequences of each species.</p><h3 class="c-article__sub-heading c-article__sub-heading--divider" id="Sec26">QTL-seq</h3><p>An F<sub>2</sub> population with 129 individuals was generated from a cross between HQ-1315 (linear-long fruits) and 1815 (round fruits), and phenotypic data on eggplant fruit length (L), diameter (D) and fruit shape index (L/D) were collected. Three mature fruits of each individual plant were selected for measurement; plants with extremely long/short fruits were selected and pooled according to the fruit length statistics. Equal amounts of DNA from the young leaves of 20 extreme individuals in each pool were mixed and sequenced. GATK 3.8 software was used to improve multiple-sample SNP and indel detection, and VariantFiltration was applied for filtering<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 86" title="McKenna, A. et al. The Genome Analysis Toolkit: a MapReduce framework for analyzing next-generation DNA sequencing data. Genome Res. 20, 1297–1303 (2010)." href="/articles/s41438-020-00391-0#ref-CR86" id="ref-link-section-d16122e3245">86</a></sup>. The SNP index was calculated with QTL-seq<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 88" title="Takagi, H. et al. QTL-seq: rapid mapping of quantitative trait loci in rice by whole genome resequencing of DNA from two bulked populations. Plant J. 74, 174–183 (2013)." href="/articles/s41438-020-00391-0#ref-CR88" id="ref-link-section-d16122e3249">88</a></sup> methods. Indel markers that were exactly the same as those of the parent were assigned an indel-index of 0, with those completely different from the parent assigned an indel-index of 1. To intuitively reflect the distribution of all indices on the chromosome, the SNP index and indel index were combined to obtain Δ(all-index). Any interval with an aΔ(all-index) value higher than the threshold at the 95% confidence level was selected as a candidate interval. SNPs and indels were annotated using ANNOVAR<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 89" title="Wang, K., Li, M. &amp; Hakonarson, H. ANNOVAR: functional annotation of genetic variants from high-throughput sequencing data. Nucleic Acids Res. 38, e164 (2010)." href="/articles/s41438-020-00391-0#ref-CR89" id="ref-link-section-d16122e3253">89</a></sup>.</p></div></div></section>
